From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

Socialist economic-political system

![Image 4](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png)This article **possibly contains [original research](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research "Wikipedia:No original research")**. Please [improve it](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit) by [verifying](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability") the claims made and adding [inline citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources"). Statements consisting only of original research should be removed._(October 2025)_ _([Learn how and when to remove this message](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Maintenance\_template\_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))_

**Authoritarian socialism**, or **socialism from above**,[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Two_Souls-1) is an [economic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_system "Economic system") and [political system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_system "Political system") supporting some form of [socialist economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_economics "Socialist economics") while rejecting [political pluralism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pluralism_(political_philosophy) "Pluralism (political philosophy)"). As a term, it represents a set of economic-political systems describing themselves as "socialist" and rejecting the [liberal-democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal-democratic "Liberal-democratic") concepts of [multi-party politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_politics "Multi-party politics"), [freedom of assembly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_assembly "Freedom of assembly"), _[habeas corpus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Habeas\_corpus "Habeas corpus"),_ and [freedom of expression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_expression "Freedom of expression"), either due to fear of [counter-revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counter-revolution "Counter-revolution") or as a means to [socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist "Socialist") ends. Journalists and scholars have characterised [several countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_non-communist_socialist_states "List of non-communist socialist states"), most notably the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China"), [Cuba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cuba "Cuba"), and their allies, as authoritarian socialist states.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntington1970-2)[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEL%C3%B6wy1986264-3)[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmandae2003-4)

Contrasted to [democratic socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_socialism "Democratic socialism"), [social democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_democracy "Social democracy"), [anti-statist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anarchist_communism "Anarchist communism"), and [libertarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libertarian_socialism "Libertarian socialism") forms of socialism, authoritarian socialism encompasses some forms of [African](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_socialism "African socialism"),[[5]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Mushkat-5)[[6]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Gregor-6)[Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_socialism "Arab socialism")[[7]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Regimes_and_Resistance-7) and [Latin American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pink_tide "Pink tide") socialism.[[8]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-CSMecuador-8) Although considered an [authoritarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian "Authoritarian") or [illiberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illiberal "Illiberal") form of [state socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_socialism "State socialism"), often referred to and conflated as _socialism_ by critics and argued as a form of [state capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_capitalism "State capitalism") by left-wing critics, those states[_[which?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid\_weasel\_words "Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words")_] were ideologically [Marxist–Leninist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninist "Marxist–Leninist") and declared themselves to be [workers' and peasants'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Workers%27_state "Workers' state") or [people's democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_democracy_(Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism) "People's democracy (Marxism–Leninism)").[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Nation_1992-9)[_[failed verification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")_] Academics, political commentators and other scholars tend to distinguish between authoritarian socialist and [democratic socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_socialist "Democratic socialist") states, with the first represented in the [Soviet Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Bloc "Soviet Bloc") and the latter represented by [Western Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_Bloc "Western Bloc") countries which have been democratically governed by socialist parties - such as Britain, France, Sweden and Western [social-democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social-democracies "Social-democracies") in general, among others.[[10]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-10) Those who support authoritative socialist regimes are pejoratively known as [tankies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tankie "Tankie").[[11]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-11)

While originating with the [utopian socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utopian_socialism "Utopian socialism") advocated by [Edward Bellamy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edward_Bellamy "Edward Bellamy") (1850–1898)[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lipow-12) and identified by [Hal Draper](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hal_Draper "Hal Draper") (1914–1990) as a "socialism from above",[[13]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-13)[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Two_Souls-1) authoritarian socialism has been overwhelmingly associated with the [Soviet model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_model "Soviet model") and contrasted or compared to [authoritarian capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_capitalism "Authoritarian capitalism").[[14]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-14) Authoritarian socialism has been criticised by the left and right both theoretically and for its practice.[[15]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarrett1978-15)

Political roots
---------------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=1 "Edit section: Political roots")]

### Socialism from above

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=2 "Edit section: Socialism from above")]

Authoritarian socialism is derived from the concept of socialism from above. Hal Draper defined socialism from above as the philosophy which employs an [elite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elite "Elite")[administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administration_(government) "Administration (government)") to run the [socialist state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_state "Socialist state"). The other side of socialism is a more democratic socialism from below.[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Two_Souls-1) The idea of socialism from above is much more frequently discussed in elite circles than socialism from below—even if that is the Marxist ideal—because it is more practical.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-History-16) Draper viewed socialism from below as being the purer, more [Marxist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist "Marxist") version of socialism.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-History-16) According to Draper, [Karl Marx](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Karl_Marx "Karl Marx") and [Friedrich Engels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Engels "Friedrich Engels") were devoutly opposed to any socialist institution that was "conducive to superstitious authoritarianism". Draper makes the argument that this division echoes the division between "reformist or revolutionary, peaceful or violent, democratic or authoritarian, etc."[[1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Two_Souls-1) and further identifies [elitism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elitism "Elitism") as being one of the six major varieties of socialism from above, among them "Philanthropism", "Elitism", "Pannism", "Communism", "Permeationism" and "Socialism-from-Outside".[[17]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-17)

According to Arthur Lipow, Marx and Engels were "the founders of modern revolutionary democratic socialism", described as a form of "socialism from below" that is "based on a mass working-class movement, fighting from below for the extension of democracy and human freedom". This [type of socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Type_of_socialism "Type of socialism") is contrasted to that of the "authoritarian, antidemocratic creed" and "the various totalitarian collectivist ideologies which claim the title of socialism" as well as "the many varieties of 'socialism from above' which have led in the twentieth century to movements and state forms in which a despotic '[new class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_class "New class")' rules over a statified economy in the name of socialism", a division that "runs through the history of the socialist movement". Lipow identifies [Bellamyism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bellamyism "Bellamyism") and Stalinism as two prominent authoritarian socialist currents within the history of the socialist movement.[[18]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lipow,_Arthur_1991_p._1-18)

The authoritarian–[libertarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libertarian "Libertarian") struggles and disputes within the [socialist movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_movement "Socialist movement") go back to the [First International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_International "First International") and the expulsion in 1872 of the [anarchists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anarchists "Anarchists"), who went on to lead the [Anti-authoritarian International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-authoritarian_International "Anti-authoritarian International") and then founded their own libertarian international, the [Anarchist St. Imier International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anarchist_St._Imier_International "Anarchist St. Imier International").[[19]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-19) In 1888, the [individualist anarchist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individualist_anarchist "Individualist anarchist")[Benjamin Tucker](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Tucker "Benjamin Tucker"), who proclaimed himself to be an anarchistic socialist and [libertarian socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libertarian_socialist "Libertarian socialist") in opposition to the authoritarian [state socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_socialism "State socialism") and the compulsory communism, included the full text of a "Socialistic Letter" by [Ernest Lesigne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ernest_Lesigne "Ernest Lesigne")[[20]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-20) in his essay on "State Socialism and Anarchism". According to Lesigne, there are two types of socialism: "One is dictatorial, the other libertarian".[[21]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-21) Tucker's two socialisms were the authoritarian state socialism which he associated to the Marxist school and the libertarian anarchist socialism, or simply anarchism, that he advocated. Tucker noted that the fact that the authoritarian "State Socialism has overshadowed other forms of Socialism gives it no right to a monopoly of the Socialistic idea".[[22]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-22) According to Tucker, what those two schools of socialism had in common was the [labor theory of value](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_theory_of_value "Labor theory of value") and the ends, by which anarchism pursued different means.[[23]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-23)

According to [George Woodcock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Woodcock "George Woodcock"), the [Second International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_International "Second International") turned "into a battleground over the issue of libertarian versus authoritarian socialism. Not only did they effectively present themselves as champions of minority rights; they also provoked the German Marxists into demonstrating a dictatorial intolerance which was a factor in preventing the British labour movement from following the Marxist direction indicated by such leaders as H. M. Hyndman".[[24]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-24) According to anarchists such as the authors of _An Anarchist FAQ_, forms of socialism from above such as _authoritarian socialism_ or _state socialism_ are the real oxymorons and the _libertarian_ socialism from below represents true socialism. For anarchists and other anti-authoritarian socialists, socialism "can only mean a classless and anti-authoritarian (i.e., libertarian) society in which people manage their own affairs, either as individuals or as part of a group (depending on the situation). In other words, it implies self-management in all aspects of life", including at the workplace.[[25]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-McKay_2008-25) Historian [Herbert L. Osgood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Herbert_L._Osgood "Herbert L. Osgood") described anarchism as "the extreme antithesis" of authoritarian communism and state socialism.[[26]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-26)

Socialists in general and socialist writers, including [Dimitri Volkogonov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dimitri_Volkogonov "Dimitri Volkogonov"), acknowledged that the actions of authoritarian socialist leaders have damaged "the enormous appeal of socialism generated by the October Revolution".[[27]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-27) While some right-wing authors have described [conservative socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservative_socialism "Conservative socialism"), [fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascism "Fascism") and [Prussian socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prussian_socialism "Prussian socialism"), among other forms of [paternalistic conservatism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paternalistic_conservatism "Paternalistic conservatism") and [right-wing politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_politics "Right-wing politics"), as authoritarian socialism,[[28]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-28) scholars have described their nature as decidedly [capitalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalist "Capitalist") and [conservative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservative "Conservative") rather than socialist.[[29]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-29)

### Utopian socialism

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=3 "Edit section: Utopian socialism")]

The economy of the 3rd century BCE [Mauryan Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mauryan_Empire "Mauryan Empire") of India was described as "a socialized monarchy" and "a sort of state socialism".[[30]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-30)[[31]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-31) Elements of authoritarian socialist thought were discerned in the politics of ancient Greek philosophers such as [Aristotle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotle "Aristotle")[[32]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-32) and [Plato](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plato "Plato").[[33]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-33) The first advocates of modern socialism favoured social levelling in order to create a [meritocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Meritocratic "Meritocratic") or [technocratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technocratic "Technocratic") society based on individual talent. [Henri de Saint-Simon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henri_de_Saint-Simon "Henri de Saint-Simon") is regarded as the first individual to coin the term _[socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism "Socialism")_.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-fsmitha.com-34) Saint-Simon was fascinated by the enormous potential of science and technology and advocated a socialist society that would eliminate the disorderly aspects of [capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalism "Capitalism") and would be based on [equal opportunities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equal_opportunities "Equal opportunities").[[35]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-35) He advocated the creation of a society in which each person was [ranked according to his or her capacities and rewarded according to his or her work](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/To_each_according_to_his_contribution "To each according to his contribution").[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-fsmitha.com-34) The key focus of Saint-Simon's socialism was on administrative efficiency and industrialism and a belief that science was the key to progress.[[36]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-36)[_[page needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing\_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources")_] This was accompanied by a desire to implement a rationally organised economy based on planning and geared towards large-scale scientific progress and material progress.[[34]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-fsmitha.com-34)

The first major fictional work that proposed an authoritarian socialist state was Edward Bellamy's novel _[Looking Backward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Looking\_Backward "Looking Backward")_, which depicted a [bureaucratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureaucratic "Bureaucratic")[socialist utopia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_utopia "Socialist utopia"). Bellamy distanced himself from radical socialist values, and in many ways, his ideal society still imitated many of the systems in the late 19th century United States. However, his book inspired a mass political movement called nationalism within the United States in the late 1800s. Those [Nationalist Clubs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist_Clubs "Nationalist Clubs"), so named because of their desire to nationalize [industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrial_sector "Industrial sector"), were strong supporters of the [populists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Party_(United_States) "People's Party (United States)"), who wanted the [nationalisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalisation "Nationalisation") of the railroad and telegraph systems. Despite their propaganda and involvement in politics, the nationalist movement began to decline in 1893 due to the financial difficulties of its main publications and Bellamy's failing health, which essentially disappeared by the turn of the century.[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-History-16) In the society depicted in the novel, private property has been abolished in favor of state ownership, social classes were eliminated, and all minimal and relatively easy work was done voluntarily by all citizens between the ages of 21 and 45. Workers were rewarded and recognized via a ranking system based on the army.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Bellamy-37) The government is the most powerful and respected institution, necessary for providing and maintaining this [utopia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utopia "Utopia").[[16]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-History-16) Arthur Lipow identifies the bureaucratic ruling of this ideal society as a quasi-military organisation of both economic and social relations.[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lipow-12) Bellamy elevated the modern military as a catalyst for national interest.[[37]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Bellamy-37)

The biggest critique of Bellamy's society is that it is based on the idea of socialism from above. The regime is imposed on the people by an expert elite, and there is no democratic control or individual liberty. Lipow argues that this inherently leads to [authoritarianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarianism "Authoritarianism"), writing: "If the workers and the vast majority were a brutish mass, there could be no question of forming a political movement out of them nor of giving them the task of creating a socialist society. The new institutions would not be created and shaped from below but would, of necessity, correspond to the plan laid down in advance by the utopian planner".[[12]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lipow-12)

In his preface to [Peter Kropotkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_Kropotkin "Peter Kropotkin")'s book _[The Conquest of Bread](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Conquest\_of\_Bread "The Conquest of Bread")_, Kent Bromley considered the ideas of [utopian socialists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Utopian_socialists "Utopian socialists") such as the French [François-Noël Babeuf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois-No%C3%ABl_Babeuf "François-Noël Babeuf") and the Italian [Philippe Buonarroti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippe_Buonarroti "Philippe Buonarroti") to be representative of authoritarian socialism as opposed to the French socialist [Charles Fourier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Fourier "Charles Fourier"), described as the founder of the libertarian socialism.[[38]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-38)

### Austrian and Chicago schools of economics

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=4 "Edit section: Austrian and Chicago schools of economics")]

While distinguishing between "voluntary and coercive strands",[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Block_2013-39) the [Austrian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austrian_School "Austrian School") and [Chicagoan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_school_of_economics "Chicago school of economics") understanding and characterisation of socialism is one based on authoritarianism and [statism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statism "Statism"). One Austrian definition of _socialism_ is based on the [state socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_socialist "State socialist") notion of "state ownership of capital goods".[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Block_2013-39) Another is that socialism "must be conceptualized as an institutional interference with or aggression against private property and private property claims. Capitalism, on the other hand, is a social system based on the explicit recognition of private property and of nonaggressive, contractual exchanges between private property owners".[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Block_2013-39)[[40]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-40)

[Friedrich Hayek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Friedrich_Hayek "Friedrich Hayek"), an Austrian School economist, was one of the leading academic critics of [collectivism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivist_anarchism "Collectivist anarchism") in the 20th century. He recognized and was acutely critical of the trends of socialism from above in collectivism, including theories based on voluntary cooperation.[[41]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ebenstein-41)[[42]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-42) Unlike Bellamy, who praised the idea of elites implementing policies, Hayek made the argument that socialism inherently leads to tyranny, claiming that "[i]n order to achieve their ends, the planners must create power – power over men wielded by other men – of a magnitude never before known. Democracy is an obstacle to this suppression of freedom which the centralized direction of economic activity requires. Hence arises the clash between planning and democracy".[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hayek-43) Hayek argued that both fascism and socialism are based in central economic planning and value the state over the individual. According to Hayek, it is in this way that it becomes possible for [totalitarian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian "Totalitarian") leaders to rise to power as happened in the years following World War I.[[43]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hayek-43) Austrian School economists such as Hayek and his mentor [Ludwig von Mises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ludwig_von_Mises "Ludwig von Mises") also used the word _socialism_ as a synonym for authoritarian socialism, central planning and state socialism, falsely linking it to fascism,[[44]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Mises-44)[[45]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-45)[[46]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-46) with Hayek writing that "[a]lthough our modern socialists' promise of greater freedom is genuine and sincere, in recent years observer after observer has been impressed by the [unforeseen consequences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unforeseen_consequence "Unforeseen consequence") of socialism, the extraordinary similarity in many respects of the conditions under 'communism' and 'fascism'".[[47]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-47) Chicago School economists such as [Milton Friedman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milton_Friedman "Milton Friedman") also equated socialism with centralized economic planning as well as authoritarian socialist states and command or state-directed economies, referring to capitalism as the free market.[[48]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-48) However, fascism and its variants such as [Falangism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falangism "Falangism") and [Nazism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazism "Nazism"), among other fascist-inspired military regimes, are considered by scholars to be a [far-right](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Far-right "Far-right"), [anti-socialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-socialist "Anti-socialist") ideologies that largely adopted [corporatist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist_corporatism "Fascist corporatism"), [liberal market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_economy#Capitalism "Market economy") economic policies, with [economic planning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_planning "Economic planning") relegated to [war efforts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_effort "War effort").[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Bel,_Gat,_Fuchs,_Fuchs-49)

Mises criticised [left-leaning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centre-left_politics "Centre-left politics"), [social liberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_liberal "Social liberal") policies such as [progressive taxation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_taxation "Progressive taxation") as socialism, getting up during a [Mont Pelerin Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mont_Pelerin_Society "Mont Pelerin Society") meeting and referring to those "expressing the view that there could be a justification" for them as "a bunch of socialists".[[50]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-50) On the other hand, Hayek argued that the state can play a role in the economy, specifically in creating a [social safety net](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_safety_net "Social safety net"),[[51]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-51)[[52]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-52) criticising the right and [conservatism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism "Conservatism"),[[53]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-53) even inspiring some towards a form of [market socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_socialism "Market socialism") or Hayekian socialism.[[54]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-54)[[55]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-55) Hayek advocated "some provision for those threatened by the extremes of indigence or starvation due to circumstances beyond their control". Hayek argued that the "necessity of some such arrangement in an industrial society is unquestioned", be it "only in the interest of those who require protection against acts of desperation on the part of the needy",[[56]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-56) with some also noting that "he advocated mandatory universal health care and unemployment insurance, enforced, if not directly provided, by the state"[[57]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-57) and that "Hayek was adamant about this".[[58]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-58) Mises also equated [central banking](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_banking "Central banking") with socialism and central planning. According to Mises, central banks enable the [commercial banks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_bank "Commercial bank") to fund loans at artificially low interest rates, thereby inducing an unsustainable expansion of bank credit and impeding any subsequent contraction.[[59]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-59) However, Hayek disagreed and stated that the need for central banking control was inescapable.[[60]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-60) Similarly, Friedman concluded that the government does have a role in the monetary system[[61]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-61) and believed that the [Federal Reserve System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Reserve_System "Federal Reserve System") should ultimately be replaced with a [computer program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_program "Computer program").[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Friedman-62) While critical of social welfare, especially [Social Security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States) "Social Security (United States)"), arguing that it had created [welfare dependency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welfare_dependency "Welfare dependency"),[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Capitalism_and_Freedom-63) Friedman was supportive of the state provision of some [public goods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_good_(economics) "Public good (economics)") that private businesses are not considered as being able to provide,[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Capitalism_and_Freedom-63) advocated a [negative income tax](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Negative_income_tax "Negative income tax") in place of most welfare[[62]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Friedman-62)[[63]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Capitalism_and_Freedom-63) and his views were grounded in a belief that while "market forces [...] accomplish wonderful things", they "cannot ensure a distribution of income that enables all citizens to meet basic economic needs.[[64]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-64) Some Austrian School economists follow Mises in arguing that policies supported by Hayek and Friedman constituted a form of socialism.[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Block_2013-39)[[65]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-65)

The Austrian and [Marxian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxian_economics "Marxian economics") schools of economics agree in their criticism of the [mixed economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mixed_economy "Mixed economy"), but they reach different conclusions regarding authoritarian socialist states. In _[Human Action](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human\_Action "Human Action")_, Mises argued that there can be no mixture of capitalism and socialism—either market logic or economic planning must dominate an economy.[[66]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-66) Mises elaborated on this point by contending that even if a market economy contained numerous state-run or nationalized enterprises, this would not make the economy mixed because such organizations do not alter the market economy's fundamental characteristics. These publicly owned enterprises would still be subject to market sovereignty as they would have to acquire [capital goods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_good "Capital good") through markets, strive to maximize profits, or at the least try to minimize costs and utilize monetary accounting for economic calculation.[[67]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-67)

Similarly, [classical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Marxism "Classical Marxism") and [orthodox](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Orthodox_Marxism "Orthodox Marxism") Marxist theorists dispute the viability of a mixed economy as a middle ground between socialism and capitalism. Irrespective of enterprise ownership, either the capitalist [law of value](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_value "Law of value") and [accumulation of capital](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Accumulation_of_capital "Accumulation of capital") drive the economy or conscious planning and non-monetary forms of valuation such as [calculation in kind](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calculation_in_kind "Calculation in kind") ultimately drive the economy. From the [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression "Great Depression") onward, extant mixed economies in the Western world are still functionally capitalist because they operate on the basis of [capital accumulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_accumulation "Capital accumulation").[[68]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-68) On this basis, some Marxists and non-Marxists alike, including academics, economists, and intellectuals, argue that the Soviet Union _et al._ were state capitalist countries and that rather than being socialist planned economies, they represented an [administrative-command system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative-command_system "Administrative-command system"). Already in 1985, John Howard argued that the common description of the [Soviet-type economic planning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet-type_economic_planning "Soviet-type economic planning") as [planned economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planned_economy "Planned economy") was misleading because while central planning did play an important role, the Soviet economy was _de facto_ characterized by the priority of highly centralized management over planning. Therefore, the correct term would be that of an economy that is _centrally managed_ rather than _centrally planned_.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-The_Soviet_Union_Has_an_Administered,_Not_a_Planned,_Economy,_1985-69) This has been attributed to both the [economy of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union "Economy of the Soviet Union") and that of [its allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc "Eastern Bloc") which closely followed the Soviet model.[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-The_Soviet_Union_Has_an_Administered,_Not_a_Planned,_Economy,_1985-69)[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ellman_2007-70) On the other hand, while describing wealthy mixed economies as still "capitalist", Austrian School economists routinely describe mixed-economy policies as "socialism". Similarly, they describe fascist regimes such as [Fascist Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist_Italy_(1922%E2%80%931943) "Fascist Italy (1922–1943)") and [Nazi Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nazi_Germany "Nazi Germany") as "socialist",[[39]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Block_2013-39) although scholars describe them as being capitalist regimes.[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Bel,_Gat,_Fuchs,_Fuchs-49)

#### Response

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=5 "Edit section: Response")]

The Austrian-Chicagoan concept of authoritarian socialism has been criticized. In particular, it has been criticised for conflating [social democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_democracy "Social democracy") and other forms of [reformist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reformist "Reformist") and democratic socialism with authoritarian and state socialism. In the United Kingdom, British [Conservative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK) "Conservative Party (UK)") politicians such as [Margaret Thatcher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher "Margaret Thatcher") "loosely labelled socialism" and conflated what "others would call social democracy, corporatism, Keynesianism or the mixed economy" with authoritarian socialism, defined as "[g]overnment support for inefficient industries, punitive taxation, regulation of the labour market, price controls – everything that interfered with the functioning of the free economy".[[71]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Campbell_2012-71) This is particularly relevant in the United States, where the term _socialization_ has been mistakenly used to refer to any state or government-operated industry or service (the proper term for such being either _[municipalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Municipalization "Municipalization")_ or _[nationalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalization "Nationalization")_). It has also been incorrectly used to mean any tax-funded programs, whether privately run or government-run.[[72]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Reinhardt_2009-72) Similarly, _socialism_ has become a pejorative used in the United States by [conservatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States "Conservatism in the United States") and [libertarians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libertarianism_in_the_United_States "Libertarianism in the United States") to taint [liberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States "Modern liberalism in the United States") and [progressive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressivism_in_the_United_States "Progressivism in the United States") policies, proposals and public figures.[[73]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Truman_1952-73)[[74]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Jackson_2012-74)[[75]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Astor_2019-75)

People such as Hayek, Mises, and Friedman have also been criticised for hypocrisy due to claiming to oppose authoritarian socialism yet supporting [liberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_liberalism "Economic liberalism")[dictatorships](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dictatorship "Dictatorship") such as that of the [military dictatorship of Chile](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_dictatorship_of_Chile_(1973%E2%80%931990) "Military dictatorship of Chile (1973–1990)") under [Augusto Pinochet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet "Augusto Pinochet"). Mises comments about fascism[[76]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-76) have been criticized,[[77]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-77)[[78]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-78) although others have defended him.[[79]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-79) Similarly, Hayek's involvement in dictatorships has been criticized.[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Farrant,_McPhail,_Berger-80) Hayek has stated: "As long term institutions, I am totally against dictatorships. But a dictatorship may be a necessary system for a transitional period. [...] Personally I prefer a liberal dictatorship to democratic government devoid of liberalism. My personal impression – and this is valid for South America – is that in Chile, for example, we will witness a transition from a dictatorial government to a liberal government".[[81]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-81) Hayek defended himself arguing that he had "not been able to find a single person even in much maligned Chile who did not agree that personal freedom was much greater under Pinochet than it had been under [[Salvador] Allende](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salvador_Allende "Salvador Allende")",[[82]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-82)[[83]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-83) the democratic socialist[[84]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-84)[[85]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-85)[[86]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-86) Chilean President democratically elected in 1970 as the first self-professed Marxist to be elected president in a country with [liberal democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democracy "Liberal democracy")[[87]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-87)[[88]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-88) and ousted in a [CIA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA "CIA")-backed [military coup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Chilean_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat "1973 Chilean coup d'état").[[89]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-89) For Hayek, the distinction between authoritarianism and totalitarianism has much importance and he was at pains to emphasise his opposition to totalitarianism, noting that the concept of transitional dictatorship which he defended was characterised by authoritarianism, not totalitarianism. When he visited Venezuela in May 1981, Hayek was asked to comment on the prevalence of totalitarian regimes in Latin America. In reply, Hayek warned against confusing "totalitarianism with authoritarianism" and said he was unaware of "any totalitarian governments in Latin America. The only one was Chile under Allende". For Hayek, _totalitarian_ signifies something very specific, namely the intention to "organize the whole of society" to attain a "definite social goal," which is stark in contrast to "liberalism and individualism".[[80]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Farrant,_McPhail,_Berger-80)

Friedman's involvement in the Chilean military dictatorship has also been criticized as he served as an economic advisor.[[90]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-90)[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-IcelandTV-91)[[92]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-92) Under Pinochet, Chile followed the economic policies of Friedman and his [Chicago Boys](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Boys "Chicago Boys").[[93]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-93)[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-94)[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-95) While Friedman did not criticize Pinochet's dictatorship at the time, nor the assassinations, illegal imprisonments, torture, or other atrocities that were well known by then,[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-96) he defended his unofficial adviser position, arguing: "I do not consider it as evil for an economist to render technical economic advice to the Chilean Government, any more than I would regard it as evil for a physician to give technical medical advice to the Chilean Government to help end a medical plague".[[97]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-97) Although Friedman criticized Chile's political system,[[91]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-IcelandTV-91)[[98]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-98)[[99]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-99) he argued that "free markets would undermine [Pinochet's] political centralization and political control",[[100]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-100)[[101]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-101) that criticism over his role in Chile missed his main contention that freer markets resulted in freer people and that Chile's unfree economy had caused the military government. Friedman advocated for free markets, which undermined "political centralization and political control".[[102]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-102) However, [some economists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miracle_of_Chile#Performance_on_economic_and_social_indicators "Miracle of Chile") have argued that the experience of Chile in this period indicated a failure of Friedman's policies, claiming that there was little net economic growth from 1975 to 1982 (during the so-called "pure [Monetarist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monetarist "Monetarist") experiment"). After the [crisis of 1982](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crisis_of_1982 "Crisis of 1982"), the state controlled more of the economy than it had under the previous socialist regime, and sustained economic growth only came after the later reforms that privatized the economy while social indicators remained poor. Pinochet's dictatorship made the unpopular economic reorientation possible by repressing opposition. Rather than a triumph of the free market, it has been described as "combining neo-liberal sutures and interventionist cures".[[103]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-103) By the time of sustained growth, the Chilean government had "cooled its neo-liberal ideological fever" and "controlled its exposure to world financial markets and maintained its efficient copper company in public hands".[[104]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-104)

Another criticism is that proponents of the theory overstate the strength of their case by describing socialism as impossible rather than inefficient.[[105]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-105)[[106]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-106)[[107]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-107) In explaining why he is not an Austrian School economist, [Bryan Caplan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bryan_Caplan "Bryan Caplan") argues that while the [economic calculation problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_calculation_problem "Economic calculation problem") is a problem for socialism, he denies that Mises has shown it to be fatal or that it is this particular problem that led to the collapse of authoritarian socialist states.[[108]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-108)[Kristen Ghodsee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kristen_Ghodsee "Kristen Ghodsee"), ethnographer and Professor of Russian and East European Studies at the University of Pennsylvania, posits that the triumphalist attitudes of Western powers at the end of the Cold War in particular the fixation with linking all socialist political ideals with the excesses of authoritarian socialism such as Stalinism had marginalized the left's response to the fusing of democracy with neoliberal ideology which helped undermine the former. This allowed the anger and resentment that came with the ravages of neoliberalism (i.e. economic misery, hopelessness, unemployment and rising inequality throughout the former Eastern Bloc and much of the West) to be channeled into [right-wing nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right-wing_nationalist "Right-wing nationalist") movements in the decades that followed.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ghodsee_2014-109)[[110]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-110)

[David L. Hoffmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_L._Hoffmann "David L. Hoffmann"), Distinguished Professor of History at Ohio State University, raises the issue of whether authoritarian socialist practices of state violence derived from socialist ideology. Placing authoritarian socialist ideologies such as Stalinism in an international context, he argues that many forms of state interventionism used by the Stalinist government, including social cataloging, surveillance, and concentration camps, predated the Soviet regime and originated outside of Russia. He further argues that technologies of social intervention developed in conjunction with the work of 19th-century European reformers and were greatly expanded during World War I, when state actors in all the combatant countries dramatically increased efforts to mobilize and control their populations. As the Soviet state was born at this moment of total war, it institutionalized practices of state intervention as permanent features of governance.[[111]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-111) Writing two _[The Guardian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_Guardian "The Guardian")_ articles in 2002 and 2006, British journalist [Seumas Milne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seumas_Milne "Seumas Milne") wrote that the impact of the post-Cold War narrative that Stalin and Hitler were twin evils and therefore communism is as monstrous as Nazism "has been to relativize the unique crimes of Nazism, bury those of colonialism and feed the idea that any attempt at radical social change will always lead to suffering, killing and failure".[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilne2002-112)[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilne2006-113)

Authoritarian socialism is a political-economic system that can be generally described as socialist, but one that rejects the liberal-democratic concepts of multi-party politics, freedom of assembly, _habeas corpus_ and freedom of expression. Other features that are common to modern authoritarian socialist states starting in the 20th century include an emphasis on [heavy industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heavy_industry "Heavy industry") for [development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_development "Economic development"), a [single-party system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single-party_state "Single-party state") to propel the goals of the [state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_(polity) "State (polity)") forward, the extensive use of [propaganda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Propaganda "Propaganda") to do the same and more.[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntington1970-2)[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEL%C3%B6wy1986264-3)[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmandae2003-4)

Soviet advocates and socialists responded to this type of criticism by highlighting the ideological differences in the concept of [freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom "Freedom") and [liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty "Liberty"). It was noted that "Marxist–Leninist norms disparaged _[laissez-faire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Laissez-faire "Laissez-faire")_[individualism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_individualism "Liberal individualism") (as when housing is determined by one's ability to pay)" and condemned "wide variations in personal wealth as the West has not" whilst emphasizing equality, by which they meant "free education and medical care, little disparity in housing or salaries, and so forth".[[114]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-114)

When asked to comment on the claim that former citizens of socialist states now enjoy increased freedoms, [Heinz Kessler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heinz_Kessler "Heinz Kessler"), former [East German Minister of National Defence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(East_Germany) "Ministry of National Defence (East Germany)"), replied: "Millions of people in Eastern Europe are now free from employment, free from safe streets, free from health care, free from social security".[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParenti1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsblackshirtsredsr00parepagen70_118]-115)

### Formation of industry

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=8 "Edit section: Formation of industry")]

As authoritarian powers enforce socialist economics, the process often goes hand in hand with supporting the growth of heavy industry as a means of reaching [industrialization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialization "Industrialization") (as can be seen with [Joseph Stalin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Stalin "Joseph Stalin")'s control of the Soviet Union). Stalin's goals brought about a rapid industrialization of the Soviet economy that increased the urban population up by another 30 million people by 1930 and the production of automobiles to 200,000 per year by 1940.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Tucker_1992-116)

Outside of the Soviet Union, two rising global participants of the early 20th century were the young states of [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany") and [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy "Italy"). Although many of the policies put in place by [German fascist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_fascist "German fascist")[Adolf Hitler](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adolf_Hitler "Adolf Hitler") and [Italian fascist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_fascist "Italian fascist")[Benito Mussolini](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benito_Mussolini "Benito Mussolini"), who also formed these [cults of personality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cults_of_personality "Cults of personality"), were contradictory and poorly understood, there were a few centrally planned work projects under their states.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-117) The [Reichsautobahn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reichsautobahn "Reichsautobahn") in Nazi Germany was an example of this. The construction of the [Autobahn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autobahn "Autobahn") and industries surrounding highway construction elevated the percentage of employed Germans throughout the construction.[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-118) In Fascist Italy, projects such as the [Battle for Grain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_for_Grain "Battle for Grain") or the [Battle for Land](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_for_Land "Battle for Land") are public work projects that socialism would traditionally support. However, the [Axis powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axis_powers "Axis powers"), among other fascist regimes, favoured a [corporatist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corporatist "Corporatist") mixed economy instead of socialism and were all radical [anti-communists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communists "Anti-communists"), [anti-Marxists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criticism_of_Marxism "Criticism of Marxism") and [anti-socialists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Criticism_of_socialism "Criticism of socialism"). Rather, they have been described as an example of authoritarian[[49]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Bel,_Gat,_Fuchs,_Fuchs-49) and [totalitarian capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian_capitalism "Totalitarian capitalism"),[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGat2007-119) with Mussolini choosing to link private businesses and the state to organize economic policies.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-120)

Common among authoritarian socialist regimes was [autarky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autarky "Autarky"). While also adopted by other authoritarian regimes, it was pursued for vastly different reasons. Authoritarian socialist states pursued autarky[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-121) to reach a [post-scarcity economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-scarcity_economy "Post-scarcity economy") to guarantee a [communist society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_society "Communist society") whereas fascist regimes pursued it for [nationalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nationalist "Nationalist") and [imperialist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialist "Imperialist") goals such as for Nazi Germany's [living space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebensraum "Lebensraum"), with [fascist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fascist "Fascist") and far-right movements claiming to strive for autarky in [platforms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_platform "Political platform") or in propaganda, but in practice they crushed existing movements towards self-sufficiency.[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-122) They established extensive capital connections in efforts to ready for expansionist war and genocide[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-123) while allying with traditional [business](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Business "Business") and [commerce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commerce "Commerce") elites.[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-124) Authoritarian socialist states and fascist regimes also differed in that the latter shifted a focus on [class conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_conflict "Class conflict") to a focus on conflict between [nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state") and [races](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_(human_classification) "Race (human classification)").[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-125)

A [Marxist societal analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_materialism "Historical materialism") puts forth that the process of industrialization in the 19th century placed the current [metropoles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metropole "Metropole") in their current positions of power. In theory, industrialization should allow the [regime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regime "Regime") of non-metropoles to raise the [standard of living](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Standard_of_living "Standard of living") and competitiveness of their [populations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population "Population") to be on economic par with these metropoles.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Keefe_2009-126) However, aside from [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia") and a number of former Eastern Bloc members, many [post-Soviet states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-Soviet_states "Post-Soviet states") and both former and current authoritarian socialist states are not categorized as [industrialized countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Industrialized_countries "Industrialized countries").[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-127)

### Single-party system

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=9 "Edit section: Single-party system")]

Authoritarian socialist states often oppose the [multi-party system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multi-party_system "Multi-party system") to instill power of the [government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Government "Government") into a [single party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_party "Single party") that could be led by a single head of state. The rationale behind this being that elites have the time and resources to enforce socialist theory because in this socialist state the interests of the people are represented by the party or head of the party. Hal Draper referred to this as socialism from above.[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Six_Strains-128) According to Draper, socialism from above comes in six strains or forms that rationalize and require an elite group at the top of a socialist system. This differs from a Marxist perspective that would advocate for socialism from below, a more pure and democratically run form of socialism.[[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Six_Strains-128)

Outside of Europe, [Eritrea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eritrea "Eritrea"), [Mozambique](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mozambique "Mozambique") and [Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vietnam "Vietnam") stand as examples of states that were socialist and ruled by a single-party at some point in the 20th century. In Eritrea, the ruling party emerging in 1970 was the [Eritrean People's Liberation Front](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eritrean_People%27s_Liberation_Front "Eritrean People's Liberation Front") (EPLF) and with control of the state the EPLF began work on socialist ideals such as broadening women's rights and expanding education.[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-129) In Mozambique, the single-state rule of [FRELIMO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FRELIMO "FRELIMO") occurred while the state was still ideologically socialist right after Portuguese rule was ending in 1975.[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-130) In Vietnam, the [Communist Party of Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Vietnam "Communist Party of Vietnam") considers itself to be in transition to socialism and also the "vanguard of the working people and the whole nation".[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-131)

### Propaganda

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=10 "Edit section: Propaganda")]

Departments of propaganda are not at all rare in these regimes. The extensive use of propaganda is spills into [art](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art "Art"), [cinema](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Filmmaking "Filmmaking"), [posters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poster "Poster"), [newspapers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newspaper "Newspaper"), [books](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Book "Book"). In the Soviet Union, a byproduct of strict [censorship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Censorship "Censorship") was the blossoming of [Russian science fiction and fantasy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_science_fiction_and_fantasy "Russian science fiction and fantasy") as well as [socialist realism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_realism "Socialist realism").[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-132) In Latin America, [Che Guevara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Che_Guevara "Che Guevara") represented and acted on the idea that socialism was an international struggle by operating [Radio Rebelde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Rebelde "Radio Rebelde") and having his station transmitted from Cuba to as far north as [Washington D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_D.C. "Washington D.C.")[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-133)

Economics
---------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Economics")]

See also: [Socialist economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_economics#Elements_of_socialism_in_practice "Socialist economics")

There are several elemental characteristics of the authoritarian socialist economic system that distinguish it from the capitalist [market economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_economy "Market economy"), namely the communist party has a concentration of power in representation of the working class and the party's decisions are so integrated into public life that its economic and non-economic decisions are part of their overall actions; state ownership of the means of production in which natural resources and capital belong to society; central economic planning, the main characteristic of an authoritarian-state socialist economy; the market is planned by a central government agency, generally a state planning commission; and socially equitable distribution of the national income in which goods and services are provided for free by the state that supplement private consumption. This economic model is greatly characterized by the government's central planning.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wilczynski-134) Ideally, society would be the owner as in the social ownership of the means of production, but in practice the state is the owner of the means of production. If the state is the owner, the idea is that it would work for the benefit of the working class and society as a whole.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-135) In practice, society is the owner only in theory and the political institutions governing society are completely set up by the state.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-136)

While [Marxist–Leninists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist%E2%80%93Leninists "Marxist–Leninists") maintain that workers in the Soviet Union and other socialist states had genuine control over the means of production through institutions such as trade unions,[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-137) democratic and libertarian socialists argue that these states had only a limited number of socialist characteristics and in practice were [state capitalists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_capitalists "State capitalists") that followed the [capitalist mode of production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalist_mode_of_production_(Marxist_theory) "Capitalist mode of production (Marxist theory)").[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Chomsky_1986-138)[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-State_Capitalism_in_the_Soviet_Union,_2001-139)[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWolff2015-140) In _[Socialism: Utopian and Scientific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialism:\_Utopian\_and\_Scientific "Socialism: Utopian and Scientific")_, Friedrich Engels argued that [state ownership](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_ownership "State ownership") does not do away with capitalism by itself,[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-141) but rather it would be the final stage of capitalism, consisting of ownership and management of large-scale production and communication by the [bourgeois state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bourgeois_state "Bourgeois state").[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Engels-142) In _[Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism,\_the\_Highest\_Stage\_of\_Capitalism "Imperialism, the Highest Stage of Capitalism")_ and _Imperialism and World Economy_, both [Vladimir Lenin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin "Vladimir Lenin") and [Nikolai Bukharin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikolai_Bukharin "Nikolai Bukharin"), respectively, had similarly "identified the growth of state capitalism as one of the main features of capitalism in its imperialist epoch".[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-143)[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-144)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-CWO_2000-145) In _[The State and Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The\_State\_and\_Revolution "The State and Revolution")_, Lenin wrote that "the erroneous bourgeois reformist assertion that monopoly capitalism or state-monopoly capitalism is no longer capitalism, but can now be called 'state socialism' and so on, is very common".[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-146)

Several economists and scholars have argued that authoritarian socialist states did not follow a planned economy, but were rather described as following an [administrative-command system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative-command_system "Administrative-command system") and called _[command economies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command\_economies "Command economies")_, a term that highlights the central role of hierarchical administration and public ownership of production in guiding the allocation of resources in these economic systems,[[69]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-The_Soviet_Union_Has_an_Administered,_Not_a_Planned,_Economy,_1985-69)[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Zimbalist_&_Sherman_1988-147)[[70]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ellman_2007-70) where important allocation decisions are made by government authorities rather than by the workers themselves and are imposed by law.[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-148) This goes against the Marxist understanding of conscious planning.[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-149)[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-150)

### Central planning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=12 "Edit section: Central planning")]

See also: [Soviet-type economic planning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet-type_economic_planning "Soviet-type economic planning")

In a [centrally planned economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centrally_planned_economy "Centrally planned economy"), there is a central planning authority usually named the State Planning Commission that is in charge of acting within the framework of social goals and the priorities designated by the party.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wilczynski-134) The planning was done under the idea that leaving market indicators would allow for social advancement.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Sirc-151) The central planning authority is responsible for five specific tasks, namely determining the criteria for the economic calculations of the planning decisions; determining and quantifying targets to be achieved within the a specified period; "coordinating targets to ensure the plan is consistent and reliable; determining the methods to ensure the realization of the plan; and revising targets in accordance to changing economic calculations.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wilczynski-134)

The planning process involved the creation of one-year plans, five-year plans and long-term plans. The one-year plans contained schedules and details that addressed current production and market equilibrium issues. The five-year plans integrated the political, military and economic strategy that would be pursued in the next five years as well as changes in capacity and production rates. It was done by a team of around the fifty leading experts from all the departments, ministries, professional and scientific organizations. The long-term plans encompassed a global strategy development. This plan was about goals for the state and society, not about individual responsibilities. Structural changes were a main theme.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wilczynski-134)[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-152) Nevertheless, centrally planned economies provided a better quality of life than market economies at the same level of economic development in nearly all cases.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Cereseto-153)

Some economists have argued that the major reason for the economic shortcomings of authoritarian socialist states which adopted Soviet-type planning was due to their authoritarian and administrative, [command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Command_economy "Command economy") nature rather than socialism itself or planning as a whole and that both economic planning and government direction of the economy through non-coercive means such as [dirigisme](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dirigisme "Dirigisme") have been practiced with success during the [post-war consensus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-war_consensus "Post-war consensus"). It has been argued that authoritarian socialist states failed because they did not create rules and operational criteria for the efficient operation of [state enterprises](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_enterprise "State enterprise") in their [administrative-command](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative-command_system "Administrative-command system") allocation of [resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Resources "Resources") and [commodities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commodities "Commodities") and the lack of [democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democracy "Democracy") in the political systems that the authoritarian socialist economies were combined with. A form of competitive socialism that rejects dictatorship and authoritarian allocation of resources in favour of [economic democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_democracy "Economic democracy") could work and prove superior to the capitalist market economy.[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-154) Others have argued that a central deficiency of such economic planning was that it was not premised on final consumer demand, but that such a system would be increasingly feasible with advances in information technology.[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-155)[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-156)

#### Economy of the Soviet Union

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Economy of the Soviet Union")]

Main article: [Economy of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_Soviet_Union "Economy of the Soviet Union")

The essence of [Soviet economics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_economics#Soviet_Union "Socialist economics") is that the [communist party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_party "Communist party") is the sole authority of the national interest. The party makes all the decisions, but they should take into account the desires of the population and these desires were then to be weighted into the decision making. According to Article 11 of its [1977 constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1977_Constitution_of_the_Soviet_Union "1977 Constitution of the Soviet Union"), the main goal of the Soviet Union was to "raise the material and cultural standards of the working people". Marxist thought and its interpretation by the Soviet Union dictated that private ownership was to be banned and the nationalization of all aspects of production a necessity, yet some things were not nationalized for the sake of economic efficiency or production targets. There was an emphasis on rapid industrialization, the development of heavy industry, relegation of consumer production as non-essential and collectivization of agriculture. Soviet-type economies also used a larger proportion of their resources on investment than do market economies. The issue with this was that current consumption was undercut because of the over-investment. All these actions supported the purposes of the state, not the people.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ader-157)

During the 1940s–1970s, the economy of the Soviet Union grew at a rate that outpaced that of Western European nations, but by the 1980s the Soviet economy was in shambles. This has been attributed to the [Era of Stagnation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Era_of_Stagnation "Era of Stagnation"), a more tolerant central government and increasing military spending caused by the [nuclear arms race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_arms_race "Nuclear arms race") with the United States, especially under [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan"), whose administration pursued more aggressive relations with the Soviet Union instead of [détente](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D%C3%A9tente "Détente") that was preferred in the 1970s. The end to the post-war consensus and [Keynesianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keynesianism "Keynesianism") in the 1970s and the rise of [neoliberalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoliberalism "Neoliberalism") and [economic globalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_globalization "Economic globalization") in the 1980s also caused problems as they forced the Soviet Union and other countries to adapt and reform themselves. Unlike China, the Soviet's failure to do so further contributed to its dissolution in December 1991.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-158) A main problem of the Soviet Union was that it pushed agriculture to the bottom of its priorities and that its central planning scheme inhibited technological innovation.[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ader-157)[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-159) Despite the attempts of the Soviet Union to guarantee employment to all of its labor force, it did not satisfy the human desires of its laborers because "people want land, not collectivization. Consumers want goods, not gigantic industrial enterprise. Workers want better wages and higher living standards, not citations and medals.
