[And] an economy cannot be politically tailored to perfection".[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ader-157)[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wellisz-160)

The Soviet Union had a poor overall performance. Although it had high growth rates in productions, many enterprises operated with losses.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lavigne-161) Nevertheless, the Soviet Union's growth in GDP per capita compared favorably with Western Europe. In 1913, prior to both [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I") and the [Russian Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Revolution "Russian Revolution") of 1917, the former Soviet Union had a GDP per capita of $1,488 in 1990 international dollars which grew 461% to $6,871 by 1990. After its dissolution in December 1991, this figure fell to $3,893 by 1998. By comparison, Western Europe grew from a higher base of $3,688 international dollars by a comparable 457% to $16,872 in the same period and reached $17,921 by 1998.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Maddison-162) From the [Stalin era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalin_era "Stalin era") to the early [Brezhnev era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brezhnev_era "Brezhnev era"), the [Soviet economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_economy "Soviet economy") grew faster than the [United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States "Economy of the United States") and maintained itself as the [second largest economy in both nominal and purchasing power parity values](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP "List of countries by largest historical GDP") for much of the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War") until 1988, when [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_Japan "Economy of Japan") took the second place.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Maddison-162) It is also claimed that the Soviet model provided a better [quality of life](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quality_of_life "Quality of life") and [human development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_development_(economics) "Human development (economics)") than market economies at the same level of economic development in nearly all cases.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Cereseto-153) With the [dissolution of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union")[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietNostalgia3-163) followed by a rapid decrease of the quality of life, there has been a growing [Soviet nostalgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_nostalgia "Soviet nostalgia")[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietNostalgia2-164) that has been most prominent in Russia[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietNostalgia1-165)[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-166) and with older people.[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietPoll3-167)[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietPoll5-168)

#### Economy of the Eastern Bloc

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Economy of the Eastern Bloc")]

Main article: [Economy of the Eastern Bloc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Bloc#Economy "Eastern Bloc")

The initial move for socialism was in 1963 after a Central Committee meeting, these countries became the [Comecon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Comecon "Comecon") countries. There were countries that chose to introduce the new economic system gradually ([Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Bulgaria "People's Republic of Bulgaria"), [East Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Germany "East Germany") and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic "Polish People's Republic")) and countries that decided to first prepare theoretically, then experimentation at different levels and then in a large scale ([Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_People%27s_Republic "Hungarian People's Republic") and [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania "Socialist Republic of Romania")). [Czechoslovakia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Czechoslovak_Socialist_Republic "Czechoslovak Socialist Republic") was set apart because the first stage of its transition consisted of economic recovery and then socialism was gradually implemented. [Yugoslavia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia "Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia") differed from other Eastern European countries in that after 1950 it modified its economic system by making self-management the base of enterprise activity.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lavigne-161) There were also a few differences between the economic model of the Soviet Union and Eastern European countries such as East Germany and Poland. Czechoslovakia and East Germany were administered along regional lines. Poland retained a centralized system similar to the Stalinist centralization of the Soviet Union.[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wellisz-160) The Eastern European countries differed from the Soviet Union in that they had greater flexibility in the management of subordinate firms, the market was assigned a greater importance, accessible foreign trade and liberalization of the exchange of capital goods. There was also less bureaucracy than in the Soviet Union involved in the planning of the countries.[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lavigne-161)

The Eastern Bloc countries achieved high rates of economic and technical progress, promoted industrialization and ensured steady growth rates of labor productivity and rises in the standard of living[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-169) despite experiencing misdevelopment by central planners.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hardt&Kaufman-170) During the 1950s–1960s, growth rates were high,[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Turnock-171) progress was rapid by European standards and per capita growth within the Eastern European countries increased by 2.4 times the European average, accounting for 12.3 per cent of European production in 1950 and 14.4 in 1970,[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Turnock-171) but most of their economies were stagnant by the late 1970s and 1980s as the system was resistant to change and did not easily adapt to new conditions.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Turnock-171) For political reasons, old factories were rarely closed, even when new technologies became available.[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Turnock-171) Growth rates within the Eastern Bloc experienced relative decline after the 1970s.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hardt&Kaufman-170) This has also been attributed to the [1970s energy crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970s_energy_crisis "1970s energy crisis"), including the [1973 oil crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_oil_crisis "1973 oil crisis"), the [1979 energy crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1979_energy_crisis "1979 energy crisis") and the [1980s oil glut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980s_oil_glut "1980s oil glut"), the [post-war displacement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-war_displacement_of_Keynesianism "Post-war displacement of Keynesianism") of Keynesianism and the rise of neoliberalism and economic globalization. Countries such as China that did not isolate and instead reformed themselves thrived, but this did not happen in most Eastern Bloc countries as they depended upon the Soviet Union, especially for significant amounts of materials.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hardt&Kaufman-170) From the end of the World War II to the mid-1970s, the economy of the Eastern Bloc steadily increased at the same rate as the economy in Western Europe, with the least none-reforming [Stalinist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stalinist "Stalinist") nations of the Eastern Bloc having a stronger economy then the reformist-Stalinist states.[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-172) While most Western European economies essentially began to approach the GDP per capita levels of the United States during the late 1970s and early 1980s, the Eastern Bloc countries did not,[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hardt&Kaufman-170) with per capita GDPs trailing significantly behind their comparable Western European counterparts.[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Hardt&Kaufman-170)

Following the fall of the Eastern Bloc with the [Revolutions of 1989](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989"), the economies of post-Soviet states quickly fell apart and took a long time to return to pre-1989 levels.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Maddison-162) Not only growth plummeted following the dissolution of the Soviet Union in December 1991, but also living standards declined, drug use, homelessness and poverty skyrocketed and suicides increased dramatically. Growth did not begin to return to pre-reform-era levels for approximately fifteen years. Some scholars have claimed that the Soviet model's industrialization and modernization laid the groundwork for their later [economic growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_growth "Economic growth"), without which their current market-oriented economy may have not thrived or growth as much, or that it provided a better quality of life than market economies.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Cereseto-153) The [1991 Soviet Union referendum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Soviet_Union_referendum "1991 Soviet Union referendum") (77% on an 80% turnout voted to preserve the Soviet Union and all [Soviet republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republics_of_the_Soviet_Union "Republics of the Soviet Union") voters voted in favor, with the [Turkmenia Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkmen_Soviet_Socialist_Republic "Turkmen Soviet Socialist Republic") showing the most support at 98% and the lowest in the [Russian Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic "Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic") at 73%)[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-173) has also been cited to argue that a vast majority of people did not want the Soviet Union dissolved, but rather more autonomy for the states within the union instead of a separation and the [massive privatizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shock_therapy_(economics) "Shock therapy (economics)") which had disastrous effects including giving rise to powerful [oligarchs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oligarchy "Oligarchy"), especially in [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_oligarch "Russian oligarch") and [Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukrainian_oligarchs "Ukrainian oligarchs").[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ther-174)[Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev"), the last [Soviet leader](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_leader "Soviet leader"), supported Scandinavian social democracy in the form of the [Nordic model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nordic_model "Nordic model").[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-175)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-176) In light of those results, post-Soviet states have seen a growing nostalgia and a constant high number of people have expressed a longing for the Soviet period and its values since the dissolution of the Soviet Union, although the level of Soviet nostalgia varies across the former republics and certain groups of people may blend the Soviet and post-Soviet experience in their daily lives.[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Kaprans-177) Polls have also showed that a majority of post-Soviet states viewed the collapse of the Soviet Union negatively[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietPoll1-178) and felt that it could have been avoided.[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietNostalgia3-163) An even greater number would openly welcome a revival of the Soviet system.[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-SovietPoll5-168)[Nostalgia for the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nostalgia_for_the_Soviet_Union "Nostalgia for the Soviet Union") has appeared in the former Eastern Bloc,[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-179) especially in eastern Germany,[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Nostalgia5-180) Poland,[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-181) Romania[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Nostalgia10-182) and the former Yugoslavia.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Nostalgia2-183)[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Nostalgia8-184)

The dissolution of the Soviet system was followed by a rapid increase in [poverty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty "Poverty"),[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet1-185)[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet2-186)[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet3-187)[crime](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime "Crime"),[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet4-188)[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet5-189)[corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corruption "Corruption"),[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet6-190)[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet7-191)[unemployment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unemployment "Unemployment"),[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet8-192)[homelessness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homelessness "Homelessness"),[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet9-193)[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet10-194) rates of [disease](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disease "Disease"),[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet11-195)[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet12-196)[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet13-197)[infant mortality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infant_mortality "Infant mortality"),[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParenti1997107,_115-198)[domestic violence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_violence "Domestic violence")[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParenti1997107,_115-198) and [income inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Income_inequality "Income inequality"),[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet14-199) along with decreases in [calorie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calorie "Calorie") intake, [life expectancy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Life_expectancy "Life expectancy"), [adult literacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adult_literacy "Adult literacy") and [income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Income "Income").[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Post-Soviet15-200) Many people in post-Soviet states felt that their lives were worse off after 1989, when capitalist markets were made dominant.[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-PewGlobal1-201)[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-PewGlobal2-202) Subsequent polls and qualitative research across post-Soviet states "confirmed these sentiments as popular discontent with the failed promises of free-market prosperity has grown, especially among older people".[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Anti-anti.communism-203)

#### Economy of China

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Economy of China")]

Main article: [Economy of China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_China "Economy of China")

The [Maoist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maoism "Maoism") economic model of China was designed after the Stalinist principles of a [centrally](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Centralization "Centralization") administrated command economy based on the Soviet model.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Marangos-204) In the common program set up by the [Chinese People's Political Consultative Conference](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chinese_People%27s_Political_Consultative_Conference "Chinese People's Political Consultative Conference") in 1949, in effect the country's interim constitution, state capitalism meant an economic system of [corporatism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corporatism "Corporatism"). It provided the maxim "Whenever necessary and possible, private capital shall be encouraged to develop in the direction of state capitalism".[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-205)

After the [20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/20th_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"), [Mao Zedong](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mao_Zedong "Mao Zedong") condemned Stalinism and the flaws in the Marxist–Leninist movement that peaked with the [Hungarian Uprising of 1956](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_Uprising_of_1956 "Hungarian Uprising of 1956"). This gave Mao space in which to experiment with departure from the Soviet socialist economy. The Maoist economic model was reliant on _High Tide of Socialism in the Chinese Countryside_, _[How to Handle Contradictions Among the People](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On\_the\_Correct\_Handling\_of\_Contradictions\_Among\_the\_People "On the Correct Handling of Contradictions Among the People")_ and _[Ten Great Relationships](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ten\_Major\_Relationships "Ten Major Relationships")_. Mao modeled the Chinese socialist economy in such a way that it led to the [Great Leap Forward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward "Great Leap Forward") and the [Commune Movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_commune "People's commune"). In _High Tide of Socialism in the Chinese Countryside_, Mao focused on the industrialization and mechanization of the countryside. In _How to Handle Contradictions Among the People_, Mao wrote about his thoughts on the problems of socialist states as well as the conflicts of interest in the Chinese socialist society. In _Ten Great Relationships_, Mao wrote about his vision of China's economy.[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-206)

The Maoist model had a dual economic goal, namely the industrialization of the countryside and the socialization of its people. It differed from the Soviet Union's goals in that Mao emphasized the [class struggle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Class_struggle "Class struggle") against the [bourgeoisie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bourgeoisie "Bourgeoisie") while the Soviet Union started advocating [peaceful coexistence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peaceful_coexistence "Peaceful coexistence"). China also allowed for more flexibility and experimentation than the Soviet Union and the countryside was at the center of its policies.[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-207) Supporters argue that life expectancy greatly improved under Mao and that he rapidly industrialized China and laid the groundwork for the country's later rise to become an economic superpower[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-O'Brien,_Gao,_Ebrey,_Galtung-208) while critics see many of Maoist economic policies as impediments to industrialization and modernization that delayed economic development and claim that China's economy underwent its rapid growth only after Maoist policies had been widely abandoned.[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Biography-209)

### Economic challenges and legacy

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Economic challenges and legacy")]

The problem with the central planning of authoritarian socialist states is that as the state develops, it also grows in complexity and the possible errors grow and the possibilities of dis-allocations and waste of resources.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Wilczynski-134) As commented by Karl Marx, capitalism works because it is a system of economic force, but in socialist economics this force is insufficient to provide enough incentive. Human needs should be taken into account to make a socialist society function, but there is no necessary connection between the accumulation of capital and human satisfaction.[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-210) Some of the issues that emerged during the socialist phase of Eastern Europe, the Soviet Union and Maoist China included inflation, lagged consumption, fixed prices, production structure and disproportionality.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Sirc-151)

There was a lag between when products were fabricated and when they were accessed to by the population, goods tended to stockpile. Yugoslavia raised its industrial prices by 17% and its agricultural prices by 32% from 1964 to 1965 while Czechoslovakia raised the prices of foodstuffs and services by 20% in 1966 and by 1967 prices were up by 30%. The production of consumer products also diminished in Yugoslavia, where the share of consumer products fell from 70% before World War II to 31% in 1965. Prices were fixed under the premise that it would force producers to behave more efficiently and as such the price-controlled products were produced in lower quantities. In Yugoslavia, the market distortion caused by the price fixing was realized and led to the un-freezing of prices in 1967. Hungary also had frozen prices and slowly unfroze them over a period of ten to fifteen years because otherwise the structural disproportions of the Hungarian economy would spin prices out of control. Many factories were kept running through government subsidies and protection despite any economic losses of the factories. This decreased overall efficiency of the socialist economies, increased the financial losses of those economies and caused them to have a disproportionate amount of available jobs and manpower. As argued by Ljubo Sirc, the "Soviet Union and other communist countries have the worst of both worlds: some enterprises or operations are inefficient because they are too capital-intensive, other enterprises or operations because they are too labour-intensive".[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Sirc-151)

The Stalinist economic model in which the socialist economies were based did not allow for a decrease in growth rates. It did not allow for the flexibility needed to keep up with growing economies.[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Marangos-204) According to [Paul Roderick Gregory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paul_Roderick_Gregory "Paul Roderick Gregory"), the [collapse of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collapse_of_the_Soviet_Union "Collapse of the Soviet Union") was due to the inherent drawbacks of the [administrative-command system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Administrative-command_system "Administrative-command system"), namely poor planning, low expertise of planners, unreliable supply lines, conflict between planners and producers and the dictatorial chain of command. According to Gregory, "the system was managed by thousands of 'Stalins' in a nested dictatorship". Once the enterprises [gained some freedom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khozraschyot "Khozraschyot") during _[perestroika](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perestroika "Perestroika")_, the rigid administrative-command system imploded.[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-211)[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-212) Despite these shortcomings, the Soviet Union's growth in GDP per capita compared favorably with Western Europe.[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Maddison-162) It has also been noted that such states compared favorably with Western states in some health indicators such as infant mortality and life expectancy,[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-213) making some significant gains and that "one thought [...] bound to occur is that communism is good for poverty removal".[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-214) A lasting legacy of the Soviet Union remains physical infrastructure created during decades of policies geared towards the construction of heavy industry and widespread [environmental destruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_destruction "Environmental destruction").[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-215) Under the Soviet system, income, property and social equality was radically increased. Income inequality in Russia dropped, then rebounded after the demise of the Soviet Union in 1991. Similarly, income inequality also dropped rapidly in the Eastern Bloc and after Eastern Europe went under the Soviet [sphere of influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence "Sphere of influence") at the end of World War II. After the collapse of the Soviet system, economic and [social inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social_inequality "Social inequality") went back up.[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-216)

The breakdown of economic ties that followed the collapse of the Soviet Union led to a severe economic crisis and catastrophic fall in living standards in post-Soviet states and the former Eastern Bloc[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-217) which was even worse than the Great Depression.[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-218)[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Russia-219) Poverty and [economic inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality") surged between 1988–1989 and 1993–1995, with the [Gini ratio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gini_ratio "Gini ratio") increasing by an average of 9 points for all former socialist states.[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-220) Even before Russia's [financial crisis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis "1998 Russian financial crisis") in 1998, Russia's GDP was half of what it had been in the early 1990s.[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Russia-219) In the decades following the end of the Cold War, only five or six of the post-communist states are on a path to joining the wealthy capitalist West while most are falling behind, some to such an extent that it will take over 50 years to catch up to where they were before the end of the Soviet system.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-221)[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-222) In a 2001 study by economist [Steven Rosefielde](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steven_Rosefielde "Steven Rosefielde"), he calculated that there were 3.4 million premature deaths in Russia from 1990 to 1998, partly blaming on the "shock therapy" that came with the [Washington Consensus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Consensus "Washington Consensus").[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-223)

According to [Klas-Göran Karlsson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Klas-G%C3%B6ran_Karlsson "Klas-Göran Karlsson"), discussion of the number of victims of authoritarian socialist regimes has been "extremely extensive and ideologically biased".[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-224) Any attempt to estimate a total number of killings under authoritarian socialist regimes depends greatly on definitions,[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-225) ranging from a low of 10–20 millions to as high as 110 millions.[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-226) The criticism of some of the estimates are mostly focused on three aspects, namely that the estimates were based on sparse and incomplete data when significant errors are inevitable; that the figures were skewed to higher possible values; and that those dying at war and victims of civil wars, [Holodomor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holodomor "Holodomor") and other famines under authoritarian socialist governments should not be counted.[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-227)[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-228)[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-229)[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-230)[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-231)[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-232) Critics also argue that [neoliberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoliberal "Neoliberal") policies of [liberalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberalization "Liberalization"), [deregulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deregulation "Deregulation") and [privatisation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Privatisation "Privatisation") "had catastrophic effects on former Soviet Bloc countries" and that the imposition of Washington Consensus-inspired "shock therapy" had little to do with future economic growth.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ther-174) It has been argued that the establishment of [welfare states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welfare_state "Welfare state") in the West in the early 20th century could be partly a reaction by elites to the [Bolshevik Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik_Revolution "Bolshevik Revolution") and its violence against the bourgeoisie which feared violent revolution in its own backyard.[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-233) The welfare states gave rise to the post-war consensus and the [post-war economic boom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-war_economic_boom "Post-war economic boom"), where the United States, the Soviet Union and Western European and East Asian countries in particular experienced unusually high and sustained economic growth, together with [full employment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Full_employment "Full employment"). Contrary to early predictions, this high growth also included many countries that had been devastated by the war such as Japan ([Japanese post-war economic miracle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_post-war_economic_miracle "Japanese post-war economic miracle")), West Germany and Austria ([Wirtschaftswunder](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wirtschaftswunder "Wirtschaftswunder")), South Korea ([Miracle of the Han River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miracle_of_the_Han_River "Miracle of the Han River")), France ([Trente Glorieuses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses "Trente Glorieuses")), Italy ([Italian economic miracle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_economic_miracle "Italian economic miracle")) and Greece ([Greek economic miracle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_economic_miracle "Greek economic miracle")).[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-234)[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-235) Similarly, [Michael Parenti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Parenti "Michael Parenti") holds that the Soviet model played a role in "tempering the worst impulses of Western capitalism and imperialism" and that Western business interests are "no longer restrained by a competing system" in the post-Cold War era and are now "rolling back the many gains that working people in the West have won over the years".[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParenti1997[httpsarchiveorgdetailsblackshirtsredsr00parepagen38_58]-236) For Parenti, there were clear differences between fascist and socialist regimes as the latter "made dramatic gains in literacy, industrial wages, health care and women's rights" and in general "created a life for the mass of people that was far better than the wretched existence they had endured under feudal lords, military bosses, foreign colonizers and Western capitalists".[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParenti1997xiii,_6%E2%80%9311,_59%E2%80%9367,_74%E2%80%9386-237)

Other have criticized the linking of all leftist and socialist ideals to the excesses of Stalinism[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDean2012[httpsarchiveorgdetailscommunisthorizon00deanpagen11_6%E2%80%937]-238)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEhms2014-239) by the elites in the West in hope to discredit and marginalize all political ideologies[[112]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilne2002-112)[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMilne2006-113) that could "threaten the primacy of private property and free markets",[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ghodsee_2014-109) emphasising Stalin and other socialist leaders' crimes and neglecting legitimate achievements such as education, literacy, the modernisation of the economy, social security, the rise in the standard of living and women's rights.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ghodsee_2014-109)[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEhms2014-239) Similarly, it has been argued that there is a double standard in emphasising famines, labour camps, mass killings and purges under socialist regimes in a death toll body count,[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-240)[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-241) but not applying the same standard to capitalist, [colonial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonialism "Colonialism")-[imperial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Imperialism "Imperialism") regimes.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ghodsee_2014-109)[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-242)[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-243) The collapse of the Soviet system, the Soviet Union in particular, is seen as the proof that communism and socialism can not work, allowing for all left-wing criticism of the excesses of neoliberal capitalism to be silenced,[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Anti-anti.communism-203) for the alternatives will supposedly inevitably result in economic inefficiency and violent authoritarianism.[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-244) Some Western academics argue that anti-communist narratives have exaggerated the extent of political repression and censorship in states under authoritarian socialist rule,[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-245) or that those states provided [human rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_rights "Human rights") such as [economic, social and cultural rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic,_social_and_cultural_rights "Economic, social and cultural rights") not found under [capitalist states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capitalist_state "Capitalist state").[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-246)

Development
-----------

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Development")]

Authoritarian socialism is best understood through an examination of its developmental history, allowing for the analysis and comparison of its various global examples. Although authoritarian socialism was by no means restricted to the Soviet Union, its ideological development occurred in tandem with the Stalinist regimes.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchulman2006-248) As the Soviet Union was a developmental model for many socialist states in the post-World War II era, Soviet authoritarian socialism was adopted by a diverse range of states and continued to develop well into the 20th century in the Middle East and North African regions. Those regions, characterized by authoritarian traits such as uncontested party leadership, restricted civil liberties and strong unelected officials with non-democratic influence on policy, share many commonalities with the Soviet Union.[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Departures_From_Post-Colonialism-249)

Authoritarian socialist states were ideologically Marxist–Leninist (the [state ideology of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_ideology_of_the_Soviet_Union "State ideology of the Soviet Union") that arose in Imperial Russia within the [Bolshevik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bolshevik "Bolshevik") faction of the [Russian Social Democratic Labour Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Social_Democratic_Labour_Party "Russian Social Democratic Labour Party")) or one of its variants such as Maoism, among other national variants and updating, following the Soviet developmental model. While those socialist states saw themselves as a form of democracy opposed to that of Western states and claimed to be workers and peasants' states or people's democratic republics,[[9]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Nation_1992-9) they are considered to be authoritarian[[2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuntington1970-2)[[3]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEL%C3%B6wy1986264-3)[[4]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAmandae2003-4) because they featured external controls such as violent repression and forms of artificial socialization.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Authoritarianism-250)

The implementation of authoritarian forms of socialism was accomplished with a dogmatized ideology reinforced by terror and violence. The combination of those external controls served to implement a normality within an authoritarian country that seemed like illusion or madness to someone removed from its political atmosphere.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Authoritarianism-250) For many authoritarian socialist countries, their regimes were a mix of this form of external control-based [totalitarianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarianism "Totalitarianism") (for intellectually and ideologically active members of society) and traditional or cultural authoritarianism (for the majority of the population).[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Authoritarianism-250)

With the [fall of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fall_of_the_Soviet_Union "Fall of the Soviet Union") and that of the Eastern Bloc, most former authoritarian socialist regimes reformed themselves. Some of those in Eastern Europe underwent shock doctrine and moved into a [free-market capitalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free-market_capitalist "Free-market capitalist") and liberal-democratic direction, although some of them such as Hungary or Russia are described as[_[by whom?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual\_of\_Style/Words\_to\_watch#Unsupported\_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")_][illiberal democracies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illiberal_democracies "Illiberal democracies") and others as [hybrid regimes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hybrid_regimes "Hybrid regimes"). In Africa, many ruling parties retained power and moved into a democratic socialist or [social-democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Social-democratic "Social-democratic") direction while others moved into liberal-democratic multi-party politics.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-251)[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-252) Other countries such as Cuba and Vietnam followed the Chinese development in applying economic reforms while maintaining centralised political control. They also include Chinese allies such as the Philippines and Thailand, who were not authoritarian socialist regimes, but are now favouring the [Beijing Consensus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beijing_Consensus "Beijing Consensus") over the [Washington Consensus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Consensus "Washington Consensus") followed by Eastern European countries.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-253)[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Kurlantzick_2013-254) Rather than moving in the direction of [democratic capitalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_capitalism "Democratic capitalism") followed by the majority of Eastern European countries, China and its allies, including Hungary, Nicaragua, Russia, Singapore, Turkey and Venezuela, are described as[_[by whom?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual\_of\_Style/Words\_to\_watch#Unsupported\_attributions "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch")_][authoritarian capitalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_capitalist "Authoritarian capitalist") regimes.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFuchs2017-255)[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFuchs2018-256)

### Soviet Union

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Soviet Union")]

Despite the Marxian basis of Vladimir Lenin's socialism, the realities of his system were in direct opposition to Karl Marx's belief in the emancipation and autonomy of the working class.[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchulman2006-248) Those contradictions stemmed primarily from Lenin's implementation of a vanguard or regimented party of committed revolutionaries "who knew exactly what history's mandate was and who were prepared to be its self-ordained custodians".[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) The function of this party was meant to be primarily transitional, given that Lenin believed that the working class was politically unprepared for rule and Russia was not yet industrially poised for socialism.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257)

Lenin adopted state-capitalist policies.[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lenin1-258)[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lenin2-259)[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lenin3-260)[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Pena-261) On seeing the Soviet Union's growing coercive power in 1923, a dying Lenin said Russia had reverted to "a [bourgeois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bourgeois "Bourgeois")[tsarist machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tsarist_autocracy "Tsarist autocracy") [...] barely varnished with socialism".[[262]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Serge-262) Marx coined the term _[barracks communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barracks\_communism "Barracks communism")_ ([German](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_language "German language"): _Kasernenkommunismus_) to refer to a form of authoritarian socialism in which all aspects of life are bureaucratically regimented and communal.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-bse-263)[[264]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-264)[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lenin_2001-265) Originally, Marx used the expression to criticize the vision of [Sergey Nechayev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergey_Nechayev "Sergey Nechayev") outlined in _The Fundamentals of the Future Social System_[[265]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Lenin_2001-265) which had a major influence on other Russian revolutionaries like Lenin and others such as [Pyotr Tkachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pyotr_Tkachev "Pyotr Tkachev").[[266]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-266) The term itself did not refer to [military barracks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_barracks "Military barracks"), but rather to the workers' barracks-type primitive dormitories in which industrial workers lived in many places in the [Russian Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") of the time.[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-bm-267) Political theorists of the Soviet Union later applied the term to China under Mao Zedong.[[263]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-bse-263) During the later perestroika period, it was applied to the [history of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Soviet_Union "History of the Soviet Union").[[267]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-bm-267)

Unlike Stalin, who first claimed to have achieved socialism with the [Soviet Constitution of 1936](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Constitution_of_1936 "Soviet Constitution of 1936")[[268]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-268)[[269]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-269)[[270]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-270)[[271]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-271) and then confirmed it in the _[Economic Problems of Socialism in the USSR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic\_Problems\_of\_Socialism\_in\_the\_USSR "Economic Problems of Socialism in the USSR")_,[[272]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-272)[[273]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-273)[[274]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-274)[[275]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-275)[[276]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-276) Lenin did not call the Soviet Union a socialist state, nor did he claim that it had achieved socialism.[[277]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-277) While Stalin's colleagues described him as Asiatic and Stalin himself told a Japanese journalist that "I am not a European man, but an Asian, a Russified Georgian",[[278]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-278) Lenin identified ethnically as Russian,[[279]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-279) believed that other European countries, especially Germany, were culturally superior to Russia[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000-280) which he described as "one of the most benighted, medieval and shamefully backward of Asian countries".[[281]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-281) From his youth, Lenin had wanted Russia to become more culturally European and Western.[[280]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000-280)[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1996-282)

In [his testament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lenin%27s_Testament "Lenin's Testament"), Lenin grow concerned about the rise of the bureaucracy and proposed changes to the structure of the Soviet governing bodies. He also made criticism of several Bolshevik leaders, including Stalin and [Leon Trotsky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leon_Trotsky "Leon Trotsky"), warning of the possibility of a split developing in the party leadership between Trotsky and Stalin if proper measures were not taken to prevent it. In a post-script, Lenin suggested Stalin be removed from his position as [General Secretary of the Russian Communist Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Russian_Communist_Party "General Secretary of the Russian Communist Party")'s [Central Committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Committee_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Central Committee of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union"). [Isaac Deutscher](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isaac_Deutscher "Isaac Deutscher"), a biographer of both Trotsky and Stalin, argued that "[t]he whole testament breathed uncertainty".[[283]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-283) Leninist socialists remain divided in their views on Stalin. Some view him as Lenin's authentic successor while others believe he betrayed Lenin's ideas by deviating from them.[[284]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService20045-284) The socio-economic nature of Stalin's Soviet Union has also been much debated, varyingly being labelled a form of [bureaucratic collectivism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bureaucratic_collectivism "Bureaucratic collectivism"), state capitalism, state socialism or a totally unique [mode of production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mode_of_production "Mode of production").[[285]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTESandle1999265%E2%80%93266-285)

#### Vladimir Lenin

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Vladimir Lenin")]

Marx chronicled a history of development through a capitalist age of industrialization that resulted in the manipulation of the [working class](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Working_class "Working class"). This development culminated in the empowerment of a [proletariat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Proletariat "Proletariat") which could benefit from the fruits of industrialization without being exploited. Although he meant his ideology to appeal to the disenfranchised working class of an industrialized society, it was widely accepted by developing countries that had yet to successfully industrialize.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247) This resulted in stagnant economies and socialist states without the necessary organization and structure to industrialize.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247) Seeing the failure of those models, Lenin concluded that socialism in Russia had to be constructed from above through party dictatorship that appealed to both the working class and peasants.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) Because the working class accounted for only 15% of the population, Lenin was forced to appeal to the much greater peasant class (accounting for nearly 80%) to propel the Bolshevik faction of Russian Social Democratic Labour Party that under Lenin eventually became the [Russian Communist Party (Bolsheviks)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Communist_Party_(Bolsheviks) "Russian Communist Party (Bolsheviks)") due to a split within social democracy.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247) The Bolsheviks promised "Bread, Peace, and Land" to the peasants and delivered, redistributing land from the landlords and increasing the number of farms in Russia from 427,000 in 1917 to 463,000 in 1919.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247)

For some, Lenin's legacy was one of violent terror and concentration of power in the hands of few.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) Lenin intentionally employed violence as a means to manipulate the population and tolerated absolutely no opposition, arguing that it was "a great deal better to 'discuss with rifles' than with the theses of the opposition".[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) He worked for the ideological destruction of society as a whole so that it could easily adopt the rhetoric and political ideals of the ruling party.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) Lenin's use of terror (instilled by a secret police apparatus) to exact social obedience, mass murder and disappearance, censoring of communications and absence of justice was only reinforced by his successor Joseph Stalin.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) In contrast to those who support this thesis,[[286]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-286) others have disputed this characterization and separated Lenin from Stalin and Leninism from Stalinism.[[287]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-287) A controversial figure, Lenin remains both reviled and revered,[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012-288) a figure who has been both idolised and demonised.[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2005-289) This has extended into academic studies of Lenin and [Leninism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leninism "Leninism") which have often been polarised along political lines.[[290]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-290) While there have been both sympathetic and expressly hostile Lenin's biographies,[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2005-289) some sought to avoid making either hostile or positive comments about Lenin, thereby evading politicized stereotypes.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012-288)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee2003-291) Some Marxist activists, who defend both the [October Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/October_Revolution "October Revolution") and [soviet democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_democracy "Soviet democracy"), emphasise how the Bolsheviks wanted to avoid terror and argue that the [Red Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_Terror "Red Terror") was born in response to the [White Terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_Terror_(Russia) "White Terror (Russia)") which has been downplayed.[[292]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-292)[[293]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-293)[[294]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-294)

Lenin has been variously described as "the century's most significant political leader",[[295]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-295) "one of the undeniably outstanding figures of modern history"[[296]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-296) and one of the 20th century's "principal actors"[[297]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2000488-297) as well as "one of the most widespread, universally recognizable icons of the twentieth century"[[298]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2005283-298) and "one of the most significant and influential figures of modern history".[[299]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan20125-299) Some historians have characterized Lenin's administration as totalitarian[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Fischer-300)[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Shub-301)[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Leggett-302)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1994-303) or a [police state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Police_state "Police state");[[302]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Leggett-302) or they have described it as a [one-party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/One-party "One-party") dictatorship,[[304]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-304) with Lenin as its dictator,[[289]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERead2005-289)[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Fischer-300)[[301]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Shub-301)[[282]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPipes1996-282)[[305]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-305) although noting differences between Lenin and Stalin in that under the first there was a dictatorship of the party and under the latter that of one man.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012-288)[[300]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Fischer-300)[[303]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1994-303) Others have argued against the view that Lenin's government was a dictatorship, viewing it as an imperfect way of preserving elements of democracy without some of the processes found in [liberal democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democratic "Liberal democratic") states.[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012-288)[[291]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee2003-291) According to the latter view, "the personal qualities that led Lenin to brutal policies were not necessarily any stronger than in some of the major Western leaders of the twentieth century".[[288]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTERyan2012-288)

Among sympathisers, Lenin was portrayed as having made a genuine adjustment of [Marxist theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marxist_theory "Marxist theory") that enabled it to suit Russia's particular socio-economic conditions.[[306]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee200314-306) The Soviet view characterised him as a man who recognised the historically inevitable and accordingly helped to make the inevitable happen. Conversely, the majority of Western historians have perceived him as a person who manipulated events in order to attain and then retain political power, moreover considering his ideas as attempts to ideologically justify his pragmatic policies.[[307]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee2003123-307) More recently, [revisionists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historical_revisionism "Historical revisionism") in both Russia and the West have highlighted the impact that pre-existing ideas and popular pressures exerted on Lenin and his policies.[[308]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTELee2003124-308)

#### Joseph Stalin

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Authoritarian_socialism&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Joseph Stalin")]

Stalin sought to rapidly industrialize the Soviet Union,[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Tucker_1992-116) but perhaps in a way that was unrealistic, given the aggregate skill level and capital of the population[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Keefe_2009-126) and Stalin's argument that the Soviet Union had to accomplish in a decade what England had taken centuries to do in terms of economic development in order to be prepared for an invasion from the West.[[309]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-309) Acknowledging this inadequacy, Stalin ordered that resources slotted for consumption be redirected to production or exported as a temporary sacrifice on the part of the population for the sake of rapid growth.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247) The model was successful initially, with ideology and nationalism promoting morale despite shortages in resources such as food and construction materials for housing. Presumably, the exploited classes believed that once the rapid and successful industrialization of Russia had taken place, power would be relinquished by the [vanguard party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanguard_party "Vanguard party") and communism would ensue.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) However, Stalin continued to demand even more far-reaching sacrifices. Because of his control over both political and economic arenas which historians argue gave his vanguard party an amount of control surpassing that of [Russia's tzars or emperors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_tsar "Russian tsar"), citizens were unwilling to challenge his decrees, given that aspects of their lives such as medical care, housing and social freedoms could be restricted according to the discretion of the party.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247)

Despite failures, Stalin's expectations remained uncontested by the working class and the model was adopted by a multitude of emerging socialist states during that era. The Soviet attempt to [collectivize agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collectivization_in_the_Soviet_Union "Collectivization in the Soviet Union"), transforming the Soviet Union from one of the world's largest exporters of grain to the world's largest importer of grain, was widely replicated despite its failure.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247) Many historians claim that extermination was the fate of a wide variety of people during Stalin's regime such as political opponents, ideological rivals, suspect party members, accused military officers, kulaks, lower-class families, former members of the societal elites, ethnic groups, religious groups and the relatives and sympathizers of these offenders.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTENugent1992-247)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchulman2006-248)[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrzezinski1989-257) Those deaths occurred as a result of collectivization, famine, terror campaigns, disease, war and mortality rates in the Gulag. As the majority of excess deaths under Stalin were not direct killings, the exact number of victims of Stalinism is difficult to calculate due to lack of consensus among scholars on which deaths can be attributed to Stalin.[[310]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-310)[[311]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-311) However, it is far lower than the estimates of 20 million or above which were made before access to the archives.[[312]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-312)[[313]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-313) Regarding the Holodomor, part of the greater [Soviet famine of 1932–1933](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932%E2%80%931933 "Soviet famine of 1932–1933"),[[314]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-314)[[315]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-315) the consensus argues that while Stalin's policies contributed significantly to the high mortality rate, it rejects the view that Stalin or the Soviet government consciously engineered the famine.[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ghodsee_2014-109)[[316]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDaviesWheatcroft2004-316)[[317]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-317)[[318]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-318) It has been argued that Stalin's "purposive killings" fit more closely into the category of "execution" rather than "murder", given he thought the accused were indeed guilty of crimes against the state and insisted on documentation.[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheatcroft19961319%E2%80%931353-319)

Among the [anti-Stalinist left](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Stalinist_left "Anti-Stalinist left") and [anti-communist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-communist "Anti-communist") Russians and Westerners, Stalin's legacy is largely negative,[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDermott2006-320) with the Soviet Union under him characterised as a totalitarian state[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321)[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKhlevniuk2015-322) and Stalin as its authoritarian leader.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKotkin2014-323) Various biographers have described Stalin as a [dictator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dictator "Dictator"),[[324]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-324) an [autocrat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Autocracy "Autocracy"),[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Conquest-325)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1991-326) an [Oriental despot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oriental_despot "Oriental despot"),[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDermott2006-320)[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDermott2006-320)[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Conquest-325) or accused him of practicing [Caesarism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caesarism "Caesarism").[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1991-326) A man who "perhaps [...] determined the course of the twentieth century" more than any other individual,[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Conquest-325) described as "one of the most notorious figures in history"[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321) and possessing "that rare combination: both 'intellectual' and killer", the "ultimate politician" and the "most elusive and fascinating of the twentieth-century titans"[[327]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMontefiore2007-327) as well as "one of the most powerful figures in human history",[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1991-326) Stalin initially ruled as part of the party oligarchy which he turned into a personal dictatorship in 1934 and became absolute dictator between March and June 1937.[[328]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-328) Stalin later built a "personal dictatorship within the Bolshevik dictatorship",[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKotkin2014-323) concentrated an "unprecedented political authority in his hands"[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDermott2006-320) and has been described as "closer to personal despotism than almost any monarch in history".[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321) Others argued that the campaigns of terror organized by Stalin were driven by his fear of counter-revolution.[[329]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-329)

Other historians and scholars cautioned against "over-simplistic stereotypes" that portrayed Stalin as an omnipotent and omnipresent [tyrant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tyrant "Tyrant") who controlled every aspect of Soviet life through [repression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_repression_in_the_Soviet_Union "Political repression in the Soviet Union") and totalitarianism,[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDermott2006-320) noting that "powerful though he was, his powers were not limitless" and that Stalin's rule depended on his willingness to conserve the Soviet structure he had inherited.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321) It has been observed that Stalin's ability to remain in power relied on him having a majority in the [Politburo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politburo_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Politburo of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") at all times.[[323]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKotkin2014-323) It was noted that at various points, especially in his later years, there were "periodic manifestations" in which the party oligarchy threatened his autocratic control.[[322]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKhlevniuk2015-322) Stalin denied to foreign visitors that he was a dictator, stating that those who labelled him as such did not understand the Soviet governance structure.[[325]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Conquest-325) Several historians have criticized the [totalitarian twins](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Totalitarian_twins "Totalitarian twins")[[109]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Ghodsee_2014-109)[[319]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheatcroft19961319%E2%80%931353-319) concept and comparisons between [communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communism "Communism")/socialism and fascism[[330]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParenti1997-330) or Stalinism and Nazism[[331]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-331) as Cold War concepts[[332]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-332) that focus upon the upper levels of society and which use have obscured the reality of the system.[[333]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-333)[[334]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-334)[[335]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-335) Others further noted how the concept became prominent in Western anti-communist political discourse during the Cold War era as a tool to convert pre-war [anti-fascism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-fascism "Anti-fascism") into post-war anti-communism.[[336]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-336)

With the collapse of the Soviet Union and the release of the archives, some of the heat has gone out of the debate and politicization has been reduced. It has been argued that the Soviet political system was not completely controlled from the center and that both Lenin and Stalin only responded to political events as they arose.[[337]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-337) Some also questioned the previously published findings that Stalin organized himself the murder of [Sergey Kirov](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sergey_Kirov "Sergey Kirov") to justify his campaign of Great Terror.[[338]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-338) Others stated that mass deaths from famines are not a "uniquely Stalinist evil" and compared the behavior of the Stalinist regime vis-à-vis the Holodomor to that of the [British Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire") (towards Ireland and India) and even the [G8](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G8 "G8") in contemporary times, arguing that the latter "are guilty of mass manslaughter or mass deaths from criminal negligence because of their not taking obvious measures to reduce mass deaths" and that a possible defense of Stalin and his associates is that "their behaviour was no worse than that of many rulers in the nineteenth and twentieth centuries".[[339]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEllman20021152%E2%80%931172-339) Despite the criticism, Stalin has been considered an outstanding and exceptional politician[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1991-326) as well as a great statesman and state-builder,[[320]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcDermott2006-320) with some suggesting that without Stalin the Soviet Union might have collapsed long before 1991 as he strengthened and stabilized the country.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321) In under three decades, Stalin transformed the Soviet Union into a major industrial world power,[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321)[[326]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-Volkogonov1991-326) one which could "claim impressive achievements" in terms of urbanisation, military strength, education and Soviet pride.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321) Under his rule, the average Soviet life expectancy grew due to improved living conditions, nutrition and medical care[[340]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-340) as mortality rates also declined.[[341]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEllman20021151%E2%80%931172-341)

Although millions of Soviet citizens despised him, support for Stalin was nevertheless widespread throughout Soviet society.[[321]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-FOOTNOTEService2004-321) Citing those achievements and highlighting crimes committed by the Western world and its leaders during the colonization and imperialist period as well as war crimes and crimes against humanity committed in the 20th century whilst arguing that Stalin's hatred came mainly from [General Secretary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union")[Nikita Khrushchev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev "Nikita Khrushchev")'s [Secret Speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Secret_Speech "Secret Speech") read during the [20th Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/20th_Congress_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "20th Congress of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union") of the [Communist Party of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union "Communist Party of the Soviet Union") in February 1956, some have attempted to rehabilitate Stalin and its legacy,[[342]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-342) or otherwise gave a more neutral and nuanced view.[[343]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-343)[[344]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-344)[[345]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-345) However, those attempts have been criticized and most of its authors labelled as _[neo-Stalinists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Stalinist "Neo-Stalinist")_.[[346]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-346)[[347]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-347)[[348]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-348)[[349]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-349)[[350]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-350)[[351]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-351) In the 21st century, more than half of Russians view Stalin positively and many support restoration of his monuments either dismantled by leaders or destroyed by rioting Russians during the dissolution of the Soviet Union.[[352]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-352)[[353]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-353)[[354]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-354) Stalin's popularity has tripled among Russians in the last twenty years[[355]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-355) and the trend accelerated since [Vladimir Putin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vladimir_Putin "Vladimir Putin"), who has been described as holding [neo-Soviet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Sovietism "Neo-Sovietism") views,[[356]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Authoritarian_socialism#cite_note-356) has come to
